        Posted 2 Feb 2007 17:42:42 UTC</td></tr><tr class="row1"><td class="postbody" colspan="2"><p>@ [AF&gt;HFR&gt;RR] ThierryH<br>
<br>
Yes - you are right - the project gets a lot of exposure to the BOINC world.<br>
<br>
During and after our AA's we have noticed several times that they get discussed on other project forums and people decide to drop in and crunch some also to see what all the fun was about.<br>
<br>
Usually after we finish an AA (Aussie Assault)many of us stay on the projects - but at less time -  because they become special to us.<br>
<br>
The science accomplished by a battle of big teams is an enormous amount, and on a new project it gives them a very good start.<br>
<br>
Our AA's are a team building and fun exercise and gets team members interested more in BOINC projects that can be done in their computers spare time instead of just wasting the cycles.<br>
<br>
It's all good fun and no one is meant to get hurt or upset - so crunch on and we'll see where we are on the 14th February when we finish this AA.<br>
<br>
Good luck everybody.<br>

The criteria for joining the <a href="http://boinc-australia.net/" rel="nofollow">BOINC@AUSTRALIA</a> team are on the first page of the team web site:<br>
<blockquote class="postbody"><b>Who can join our team?</b><br>
<br>
Whether you are contributing a little to one project with one old computer or participate in several projects with a building full of the latest equipment, we welcome your contribution.<br>
<br>
While our emphasis is on Australians living anywhere in the world (including Australia) and anyone living in, or having some connection with Australia, <b>anyone</b> is welcome to join us.</blockquote><br>
<br>
Australian is a prime choice for migration, so we are very used to numerous cultures, ethnicities, nationalities and religions. Our biggest war hero (Simpson and his donkey) was Dutch born I think. With over 240 nationalities(1) represented here, we've become acustomed to living with people from all over the world and having Australians living all over the world.<br>
<br>
The Danish even have one of our <a href="http://www.crownprincecouple.dk/ac000c/GSID/6140451" rel="nofollow">Princesses</a> and Hollywood has most of our actors.<br>
<br>
So attracting members from anywhere in the world seems natural to us. As natural, I would have said, as 	L'Alliance Francophone having Australian team members. ;-)<br>
<br>
Cheers.<br>

        Posted 4 Feb 2007 16:49:30 UTC<br>Last modified: 4 Feb 2007 16:54:31 UTC</td></tr><tr class="row0"><td class="postbody" colspan="2"><p>For the record, I am the guy who has "China" for a country. I've lived here the past 8 years or more, and I like the place so I crunch for China. But I'm also an Australian and so I crunch for BOINC@AUSTRALIA. Besides, I am at a bit of a disadvantage in the forum of BOINC@CHINA. :-) (Although at less of a disadvantage that I would be at on the AF forum.)<br>
<br>
But I think the membership wishes (there aren't any rules, because anybody can join or leave any team)do state that anybody who feels like joining BOINC@AUSTRALIA for any reason is free to do so. We will welcome any cruncher with open arms as long as they don't abuse people or use bad language on our forum. Oh, and we don't particularly welcome people who cheat on credits because that's bad for the goals of the team - to have a bit of fun and help science on the way. <br>
<br>
That said, we only *actively try to recruit* people who are not currently a member of any team, (Australian or Not) and who we think for some reason have some connection with Australia. But that said, the great majority of our members (including me)chose BOINC@AUSTRALIA without being recruited, and we hope that they will stay because they like it here. We welcome any cruncher who chooses us, regardless of  their native language or country, whether they have an acre of supercomputers or one Pentium III, and whether they crunch with us for one week or 5 years. We are grateful for the time we are able to walk beside anybody!<br>
<br>
The whole idea of Aussie Assaults is to have a bit of fun and create a bit of fun for the team members who like that kind of thing. About 10% of our team members actually take part in that sort of thing. Part of the fun is a bit of friendly rivalry between teams, but it is certainly not our intention to upset people. I still think that 99% of the Alliance Francophone are having fun. Let's face it AF have put up a magnificent effort of rallying the troops and at the moment are teaching us a thing or two.<br>
<br>
But let's not get too serious, folks. If this is not fun for you anymore, regardless of which team you are on, it is your choice to do something else and we will respect you for that and not reproach you at all. Let's face it, we are giving up time, money, sleep, grades and in many cases losing conjugal privileges for this. It had better be fun!<br>
<br>
Me? I'm having a whale of a time! And I'm off to work on that lazy Core 2 Duo. I reckon I can squeeze another 100 credits a day out of its sorry chassis. :-)<br>
<br>
live long and crunch.<br>
<br>
--miw<br>

Does anyone here remember seeing a Paul Newman film (with Robert Redford) called 'Butch Cassidy and the Sundance Kid'?<br>
After Butch and Sundance have robbed a train, the Sheriff and his posse follow the two outlaws for mile after mile, day after day, never letting up the pressure.<br>
At one point, Butch (Paul Newman) sees the posse in the far distance, still in pursuit and says <b>'Who are those guys?'</b><br>
<br>
Similar situation here - AF are Butch and Sundance, B@A are the posse......<br>
<b>'Qui sont ces type?'</b> (apologies for the translation!)<br>

Joined: Jan 21, 2007<br>Posts: 32<br>ID: 1770<br>Credit: 2,777,039<br>RAC: 505<br></span></div></td><form action="forum_rate.php?post=1555" method="post"></form><td colspan="2" class="postheader"> <a href="forum_thread.php?id=76&amp;nowrap=true#1555">Message 1555</a> - 
        Posted 6 Feb 2007 3:13:29 UTC</td></tr><tr class="row0"><td class="postbody" colspan="2"><p>Hmm. Unless you have been reading the internal threads, I doubt you can know exactly what the goals of an AA are. In fact, we don't even know because everyone in the team has a slightly different idea in mind. But perhaps I can give you an insight into how we choose the targets for AAs (up to now, at least.) <br>
<br>
As Webmaster Yoda said, planning for AA5 started in December and the choosing was well under way in the 2nd week of January. Everybody has a different idea of which project we should boost in an AA5, so we vote. Things that get taken into consideration by different people include quality of the science on the project, the stability of the servers, whether the project admins are active, whether cheating is under control in the project, whether we can improve our position (yes - a shot at #1 captures a lot of people's imagination, but if that was the only condsideration we would probably not have gone for ABC this time, and last time we took on SETI where we didn't even have a shot at #40!), availability of clients for platforms other than windows, fairness of credit, etc etc etc. One thing that comes way, way down the list is who is ahead of us in the project. (Although you guys have been such good sports, we are AT THIS VERY MOMENT looking for other projects where we might tweak your tails in mini assaults.) :-)<br>
<br>
As to whether an AA is successful, there are many figures of merit. Obviously getting to #1 would be nice, but it is not even the most important consideration. During the runup to AA5 and through the first week, a bunch of people have joined B@A. That's good. A bunch of B@A members who had stopped crunching have started again. That's better. Members have worked out how to squeeze another 50 credits/day out of their PC's sorry chassis and B@A's total output has gone up more than 10% in the past month. That's totally marvellous. Many of us have gone without sleep, food and other creature comforts for a week. That sucks, but 3 out of 4 ain't bad. Oh. and we are having a lot of fun and the forums are active. That's probably the main thing.<br>
<br>
Looks like AA5 has had a positive effect on the AF team's output as well. Since in the end, although we may compete from time to time, we all crunch side by side towards the project goals, that's good too.<br>
<br>
But if you want to define success and failure in your own terms, you are welcome to your own opinion, of course.<br>
<br>
--miw<br>
<br>
____________<br>

The average gap in pace between AF and B@A is about 4500 credits per hour (based on the last 12 hours). That's an extrapolated RAC gap of 108 000 credits.<br>
<br>
En franais :<br>
L'cart moyen de rythme entre l'AF et les Aussies est d'environ 4500 crdits par heure (sur les 12 dernires heures). En extrapolant ce chiffre cela fait une diffrence de RAC de 108 000 crdits.<br>

<br>
I want to thank everyone in AF for the manner in which the "battle" has been conducted. The way in which you managed to muster so much support within your team and increase your output so significantly was quite extraordinary and very impressive to watch. Because of it, we have exceeded our wildest expectations for AA5. Our most optimistic predictions had us totalling 1.1 million credits with about 60 team members involved. We actually managed nearly double both figures, and this would not have happened without the magnificent response of AF!!<br>
<br>
The fact that both teams managed to get around 10% of their members on ABC is impressive.<br>
<br>
I particularly want to thank ThierryH for starting this thread which fired us all up so much, and also Ivan leFou for the great work on the stats pages that made such great reading (even if they did contain the odd "dig" at us! :-)<br>
<br>
As Hendrik has said, between us we did great things for ABC@Home.<br>
<br>
Thanks also to those crunchers that joined us, either permanently or temporarily, during AA5. The publicity the AA5/AF rivalry attracted can only be good for BOINC.<br>
<br>
Congratulations to both teams, and thanks again for a fun two weeks.<br>
<br>
Oh, and thanks, but I'll pass on the medal you made for us! :-)<br>
